Seems to me the best thing ravers can do, as ravers, is to continue to make
harmony and promote tolerance and openness to everyone. We all have our
politica
l lives as well, of course.  And what we do there follows that star of our
individual consciences.  But rave music, like the best of 60s rock, is meant to
affirm and bring together. To let it get tangled up in the crosswebs of hate
and frustration would be a mistake. To let raves be what they are is to join
the forces of healing.
  To rave is to affirm.

Subject: Thursday night curfew
Status: R


Last night, 2 of the three raves going on were cancelled.  The only
one left was Terriculous Imagination at the Endup which had the right
setup and everything.   The DJjs were playing music that was fierce,
the interactive video was fun to see how one's movements
translated to the video and Frank Genius was creating some amazing
live techno right in front of me.  I loved his sets and his songs really
hit the right note because I love house that have "rests" in a song
where you can only hear the piano or other ambient lull.    

The atmosphere was really good.  It's just too bad that more ravers
didn't venture out and become part of the "safety zone" within the
confines of the curfew.  It was kind of like a twilight zone because
all businesses including gas stations that I drove by south of Market
last night were closed.  Motorcycle cops were parading down the street
in convoys of 6 or 7 (not stopping for red traffic lights) about every
half hour or so, I think.  Outside some ravers who decided to use the
phone in the unlit Shell gas station opposite the Endup got harrassed
and scared by the police.  BUT INSIDE, the music was going on and it
felt like a safety zone from the harshness outside (mostly due to cops).

If only more ravers had not sat in front of their TVs watching the
news and had come down instead, it would have been really on fire. 
Of course, I'm not endorsing breaking the curfew.  I'm just saying I
did and I was glad that I did. :-)  I think Terricolous Imagination is
coming back some time in the next month or two.

happy raving 

- TAXI

I wonder what TV viewers in the rest of this world think of the
American Justice system.  In their news reports, first they see a
video clipping of a man being beaten by cops in the US, then they hear
that these cops are declared innocent, and then they see news reports
of massive riots, fires, and dozens dead.  I wonder if they are
shaking their heads.  The American legal/justice system: what a gem?!?
I hope no other country in this world models their justice system on
the one in this country.

spraypainting, etc.  it's funny, here, and in town, when the students go 
out to protest/fuck shit up the cops just race ahead of the crowd and stop
traffic for us.  never arrests.   

anyway, the mob headed downtown and thrashed the police station.  we
busted the glass doors and threw bricks thru their windows.  slogans
and crossed-out swastikas were spray painted all over the building, and
a flag was burned on the sign in front.  again, the cops just stood by.
we even ripped some of the security bars off their windows.

so we left city hall and went to the courthouse to break more windows.
unfortunately, the sherrifs kept us from actually getting into the courthouse.
it would have been /great/ to get in there and thrash stuff.

it's really hard to riot at ucsc.  they (reagan) designed it that way.
it took an hour to walk en masse to the police station, and 45 minutes 
to walk thru all eight colleges.

I loved it, even though it got closed down early.  Neat meeting point,
good warehouse (sound reverberated quite well!), heat&humidity made it
comfortable, no alcohol (my first rave where no alcohol was served --
this had a profound effect on how the participants participated -- it
was great!)  The cops came in sometime in the night and closed it
about half way through -- perhaps they had ligitimate concerns about
fire safety codes, but seriously there was very little to burn and two
big gates to run out of in case of danger.  Plus, the DJ was right
next to the only wooden wall -- fast notification!  But alas we were
all referred to Townsend, for half price ($5).  (btw equinox was $10)

I also loved Care*Free right afterwards.  Really good crowd, great DJs
-- for me anyway.

Hope to see you all again soon!

-ulmo

From bbehlen Sun May  3 17:32:59 1992

Subject: Great picnic!

	It was great! The sound system sounded better than I thought it would,
helped by the fact that we had great DJ's working the tables. There was more 
than enough food, and someone had the incredible foresight to bring colored
pens and stickers to customize the buttons with. All in all a very warm and
friendly event, and it was terrific to finally put faces together with all 
these e-mail addresses. 

	So do we want to hold another one of these, in a month or so? If we
do, I won't be able to arrange it, since I'll be out of town from May 23rd
until the end of June. If someone wants to volunteer to be the organizer,
by all means make yourself heard. It's really not that much trouble, just a
little nerve-wracking.... GG Park sounds like a great place to hold it. I
don't know the park that well, so I can't help in the location decision, or
where would be ideal for the sound system. All I know is, if you need a permit
look into it early, so we can make sure we have it and that the place is
reserved. Also, we might want to think about inviting other people to attend - 
people we know love the music and are friendly enough to want to meet others.
It would be interesting to see if we could get 100+ people and still maintain
the atmosphere...

	Also, many people who contributed money to help pay for the reservation
and permit asked me to tell the list how much I lost if I didn't break even.
I wasn't forceful at all in collecting the money, but I think it would be 
unfair to those who did help out to not ask everyone to pay. People gave me $76
out of the $130 it cost for the site. If you went and enjoyed it, and either
forgot to pay or didn't know who to pay, you could send me $2 or so in the 
mail. I'll post my address at the bottom of this letter. I feel like Jerry
Falwell or Jimmy Bakker.....

	Finally, I have some bad news to report. SFRaves will have to move
soon, by the end of the month, because my sysadmin-friend lost his job
(actually, the machine's being moved to a different department, with their 
own computer staff), and I'm in the process of looking for a new machine here
on campus. The OCF, a free student-run cluster of Apollos, has offered to
distribute the list over the summer, so as soon as I transfer some files and
am ready, I'll send let the list know. Over the summer I should be able to
set the list up at either soda or garnet, so I'll let you know. If worst
comes to worst, I'm willing to let someone on the list assume control, and
set it up at their machine. I really like being the list admin, so I
would really prefer to find a machine here I can use... like I said, I'll
keep y'all posted.

	Cheers, and thanx for the great picnic!

	Brian Behlendorf
	2601 Warring St. #12
	Berkeley, CA 94704
	(until May 23rd)

 ************************************************************

 I was only able to make it to the last 1.5 hour of the first ever sfraves
picnic. Still, I had a good time. It was strange to dance on the uneven
forest floor. If you tried to do anything that involved only one foot on
the ground, it was easy to lose your balance. It made it hard to do spins.

 Thanks to the good DJs that risked the life of their vinyl to the cloud
of dust we raised.

 Neat light toys, brought by **** ( I don't remember her name, the gal
from WELL w/ 2 kids ). Kaleidoscopes of all kinds. And who brought the
blow-strobe mask? I copied the address from the inside of the mask:

         "Send $14.95 to:  Alpha Odysseys
                           PO Box 17997
                           Boulder, CO 80308

 Before I send $14.95 to these guys, I was wondering if this thing is still
available locally? Where have people found them?

 Definitely send Brian $$$ for the picnic, if you've not done so ( like me -
there was this nagging thought at the back of my mind, all the time I was 
at the picnic ...).

 Hopefully, by the time of the next sfrave picnic, I'll have completed a
working model of a "stereo" LED strobe goggle I've been designing. It's
inspired by an experience I had a few months ago. I was at a "cyber" event
in Santa Cruz, and in one of the rooms, they had put out a bunch of hand-
held LED flasher units. I took one in each hand, and held them up against
my closed eyelids. Having different frequencies going to each eye is quite
different from having the same frequency - "stereo" vs "mono". If I ever
get this goggle made, I'd like to find out what other people experience
when they use it!

                                                Larry Ching

>  Hopefully, by the time of the next sfrave picnic, I'll have completed a

Hmm, looks like you're heading towards mind machine country.  I have a
machine called the "Shaman" that may do some of what you are designing
... the effects can be very interesting.  There're a couple of books
on this that could be stimulating to some subscribers of this mailing
list; "Would Buddha Wear a Walkman?" & the much earlier "Mega Brain".

There is also a now-quiet mailing list called "mind-l" that used to
have a fair amount of traffic on building machines like this,
reviewing products that appeared, organizing group buys, & the like.
I don't think anything happened to it, the audience stopped posting.
However, it still exists & the archives, resource guides, FAQ, & so on
still exist, & are available via anonymous ftp on asylum.sf.ca.us.
The mailing list is mind-l@asylum.sf.ca.us.  There is some form of
listserv running so I think the proper way of subscribing is to mail
to listserv@asylum.sf.ca.us.

Sorry if I'm preaching to the choir here but if there was ever a
better target audience ....

Oh & b-rave-o for the picnic & site, Andrea, Brian, & everyone else
who worked on the arrangements; it will sure be hard to beat or even
match the location (do try!), & it was great meeting y'all.

To: sfraves@petrus.berkeley.edu

Subject: Crunch Berrie Rave, Seattle
Status: R


Sorry, would have given advance notice but I just found out about this 
one the night it gave birth (Saturday 5/2).  At any rate, here's the scoop.

It was GREAT!!!!  It was across the street from the ReBar (a really 
outrageous club in its own right, best on Thursdays), in this building 
that is a ramp-up flat level parking garage above and just a huge 
enclosed empty space underneath, big enough for several skateboard 
ramps.  I got there about 1:40, just before the line got really huge 
from all of the clubs letting out.

The GyroTrons they had are pretty crazy.  Picture five hula hoops of 
different sizes, arranged in concentric rings (somewhat like the orbit 
of the planets around the sun).   Each ring is connected to the next 
ring inside of it.  You stand spread-eagled (much like DaVinci's 
diagram) in the center hoop, feet on one side and hands holding the 
other and there is a harness that locks around your waist, holding you 
in place.  Then the operator starts spinning the exterior hoop against 
its axis (so it cuts a spherical pattern in the air), causing each of 
the internal hoops to spin similarly, but in different direction.  You, 
in the center hoop, first go head over heels, and start twisting 
sideways, backwards, rotating left to right in a totally unpredictable 
fashion.  There were two of these things operating on different sides 
of the space, and there were huge lines to each of them.  Looked like 
tons o' fun.  I'm going to try them out at the next Captain Crunch rave 
(in about 3 weeks).

The music was great;   DJs were Dominator from Seattle and Maxi and 
Devistator from LA and they CRANKED.  This rave just had one set of 
tables operating at a time (which was logistically elegant--the DJ had 
total control over the sound in this wide open space).  The sound 
stacks were about 8 feet high and thirty feet long, all told.  The air 
had a physical presence from the sheer sound these guys were putting 
out.   The smart bar seemed pretty cool.  They didn't serve alcohol 
which decomplicated things considerably and no one seemed to need it 
anyway.  The only neg was the facilities challenge, which was a noxious 
hassle.  Everyone there was having a ridiculously great time.  Met a 
lot of people there I knew and have the goods on three of four 
different raves happening up here in the next three weeks.

	Satta.

		>>Dread-Eye

"Getting along with women,
Knocking around with men,
Having more credit than money,
Thus one goes through the world."
 Claudine von Villa Bella [1776]
Johann Wolfgang von Goethe   1749-1832

P.S.  Seattle's been going through its own pains on the spontaneous 
combustion/mob psychology violence score, but it's been pretty minimal. 
 We've had a number of demonstrations involving shutting down the 
freeways with hundreds of protestors and protesting in front of the 
main Administration buildings for the seat of the county government.  
It's been random innocent-business owner-victimizing- window-breaking 
stupidity and one apartment complex got torched.  But on the upside, 
the whole thing sure has gotten a lot of people talking.

Nicely put... This is NOT the place for flames.  It just detracts from the fun
and informative purpose of the list.  Plus it tends to degrade what I feel is
a growing sense of community among us sfravers!

> >I apologize for using this mailing list for this purpose.
> 
> ditto.  It's getting too politically correct around here for my tastes.

YES!  This is not a newsgroup, but rather a means for all of us on the mailing
list to interact and communicate and inform each other.  Vitamin B  could
 verify this, but I'm willing to bet that there are less than 200 people
subscribed to the list.  Obviously we, the sfraves subscribers, share a common
interest, i.e. the desire to rave.  That is what we should focus on on the
list...info and discussion of raves.  Any opinionated posts, flames, etc 
would be better sent to alt.rave or elsewhere.  The list is not a place to
share our differences, but rather a means for us to explore our common
interests and (if we're lucky) to get to know each other...

Okay, umount /dev/preachy.soapbox...I'm *glad* that the police didn't make it
too hard for the ucsc protesters, that way no one gets hurt.  Property damage
can be repaired...Let's not judge each other's means of political expression.
If we MUST be political on this list, let's discuss ways to politically 
influence the world in a positive manner using the friendly outlooks that 
(good) raves generate!

-Howard

Thanks for the compliment.  I'm known to flame quite a bit myself,

have a mutually-consenting-adults-flame kind of relationship with.
(Partha ?)

>YES!  This is not a newsgroup, but rather a means for all of us on the mailing
>list to interact and communicate and inform each other. 

Yes, on sfraves there's been a tendency to jump on other people.
I suspect the people jumping have never made complete idiots of
themselves the way I have via flaming.  I learned a lot
by making a fool of myself for an audience.  It's embarrassing.
Now, I try to stay quiet until I've been able to think the
issues over a little bit.  I've had to apologize/say I'm
sorry/say I'm stupid less frequently.

For example, the recent discussion of whomever it was being
approached by a transexual.  Well, it startled the person,
and effected his/her impression of the place being described.
So what ?  I'm a woman too, and I know how intolerable some men
can be, but so what ?  You learn to deal with it eventually.
Women can be pretty intolerable sometimes too.

>If we MUST be political on this list, let's discuss ways to politically 
>influence the world in a positive manner using the friendly outlooks that 
>(good) raves generate!

I find it hard to disagree with this statement, but all we can do is
try, and people can flame away to their hearts' desire.  It's just,
well, if it gets personal, please take the war to e-mail, and just
cc in everyone who's involved.  Where I come from, it's considered
adult-like to suggest that something be taken to e-mail by
one of the parties involved before it gets too personal.
The list rarely wants to hear about it.

So, I'm obviously procrastinating on a project due last week.

I'll try not to make a habit of philosophizing on sfraves.

Come-Unity should be fun.  It started about a little over a year ago, and was
really hot last summer, every Tuesday night.  It sort of wound down last fall,
but they've started them up again roughly once a month.  You can almost count
on most of hard-core rave kids to be there, and the music will be great, with
Jeno and Garth spinning.

I went last month and had a fun time -- it was almost as good as last summer. 
There were a few times last summer when it hit critical mass and the entire
place was screaming and whistling and dancing hard.  Up to then, I had never
seen such a high energy level.  It starts picking up around 12:30 and the
energy level keeps increasing up until 2:00 or 3:00.

It's a cool space -- they use just the lower back dancefloor at 1015 folsom. 
The room is just the right shape for concentrating the dancing energies.  Not
too big, not too small, and the high ceiling adds volume.  The sound system is
one of the best around and the lights are fantastic.  They've even added a
chill out room.  Definitely a good time.

Check it out if you have the chance.

Tim

From: Desi The Three-Armed Wonder Comic <jondr@sco.COM>

this article is from `Public Eye' section of The Metro, april 30-may 6
edition.  i have no idea how true most of it is, but it seems
sympathetic to the rave cause, and it is an interesting account of
what happened to Intemperance & Destiny's doomed `Deep Rooted House'
event.  For some reason, the paper likes to uses ellipses (...)
rather than paragraph breaks.  I have rectified this.

CRIME RAVE: Although it's facing a dramatically reduced budget, the
county Sheriff's Department apparently has no qualms about spending
large amount of public cash to bust illegal dancers.

Around 1 AM Sunday morning, 15 deputy sheriffs swept into Saratoga
Springs and attempted to shut down a Woodstock-like dancefest that was
billed as Northern California's first-ever outdoor ``rave.''  The
Sheriff's Department says the bash was illegal because its organizer,
San Jose mechanic Steven Cohen, had failed to obtain the required
permits.  According to county ordinance B-3112, it's a crime to throw
a dance party without government permission.

Pulling the plug on the rave, however, proved to be a logistical
nightmare.  Most of the youths who attended the event (admission was
$15) had been ferried to the rave by a shuttle service that operated
between the resort area and Saratoga High School.  To take them back
to their cars, the Sheriff's Department hired three county transit
buses, and a transit supervisor.

Still, the party-goers boogied well into the night.  When deputies
ordered disc jockeys to turn off their amplifiers, the crowd kept the
beat going by banging on cowbells, clapping hands and blowing
whistles.  At one point several hundred sweaty youths -- many sporting
huge Mad Hatter-type hats and swaying rhythmically to the digitized
syncopations of high-tech ``house'' music -- gathered around a Honda
Civic equipped with an Alphasonic sound system and 12 Cerwin Vega
speakers

By 3 AM the party was pretty much over, except for a few ravers who
camped out.  There was only one arrest.  Later that morning, Cohen was
busted on an outstanding warrant stemming from a previous party in San
Jose.  He was released Monday.  Sheriff flakkie Sgt Ken Kahn tells us
the department intends to make Cohen pay for the cost of policing the
rave.  Kahn couldn't provide an exact figure, but he says sheriff's
deputies usually charge $24 an hour.

Cohen, meanwhile, says he plans to sue the owners of Saratoga Springs.
He charges that it was their responsibility to have the required
paperwork, not his.  ``If I knew that they didn't have a permit, I
could've gotten one myself for 25 bucks.''

Jon Drukman (finely honed machine)              uunet!sco!jondr   jondr@sco.com
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Always note the sequencer - this will never let us down.

From: bill coderre <bc@apple.com>
Message-Id: <9205061917.AA29022@apple.com>
To: sfraves@ocf.Berkeley.EDU
Subject: On Mail and Mandibles, or How to Have Fun
Status: R

One thing that I have found to be true from my own experience, and
have since found to be especially true of the Rave experience, is that
the party is always in your mind, first and foremost.

To wit: calling this or that "rave" or "b&t", or deciding that this is
"house" and that "techno", is really a reflection on the appellator as
much as the object.

Rave is not about objectivity. It is a subjective experience that
cannot be shared, only mutually experienced. Appellations are
meaningless. You can't take a photo of a hallucination, and you can't
make a firm distinction between Category A and Category B, especially
with a world full of Maxwell's Demons (some call them artists) busy
blurring the distinguishing lines as fast as you can draw them.

This may seem obtuse, but it brings up two crucial points about this
mailing list:

1) Arguing about distinctions is difficult, since so-called "objective
reality" is a delusion -- hopefully shared by the person you are
talking with. With Rave, it is even more futile, for reasons above.

One might wonder, therefore, why people insist upon fighting about
these distinctions -- especially on this list.

2) One doesn't go to the Rave, one brings the Rave with them. If you
have difficulty with transporting an attitude, might I suggest that
the next time you go out, you should bring friends and toys to provide
a layer of psychic insulation to protect your rave mindset.

The wise student will realize that he is the creator of the fun, not
the consumer, and therefore will do well to make the fun happen, as
opposed to measuring it in watts and metres, and by measuring finding
it wanting.

professor HEINOUS
"I always have fun because I am out of my mind" -- Zippy

ps. Please realize that this list generates about 100 mail messages
per week. Each message takes several minutes of several hundred
peoples' time, so effectively the list, as an entity, consumes enough
time to keep 5-10 people employed full-time. Please do your part to
make sure that that time is used effectively.

I don't know about y'all, but I had a great time. Thanks to Tim H. and
others that recommeded this rave.

Basically, I liked the atmosphere: the crowd seemed friendlier than some
other raves I've attended. The size, IMHO, was just right -- I never liked
huge crowds and cavernous halls that much anyways. Chill out rooms provided
safe haven against an occasionally relentless techno mindfuck. Music was
mostly excellent, modulo a few rough and ragged cuts, and a few places
where the beat was too simple&monotonous. $5.00 price was right.

Party people in the house listen up -- Please tell us when/where the next
one is happening!

			"Music so loud... can't tell a thing!"
					Alex Chilton / Big Star.

So I walk into the Top
because it's open again
but my mouth had to drop
because it looks so plain.
The red curtains are gone
and the wall paintings have changed
the music is raggae  blah blah lawn.
blah, blah, blah, blah, blah schmanged

arrrrrggghhhhhh *#!@ the poem, it's too much work......

So I walk into the Top and it sure has changed.  I went there last night 
(Tuesday) and the music now is raggae.  The new managers repainted the walls
from red to white and brown, I think.  They took off the old paintings and 
hung new ones up.  They took down all the red curtains hanging between the 
dance floor and the main floor and those hanging behind the front windows 
facing the street, and shazoooooom!, suddenly the place doesn't look anywhere 
near as cozy as it used to.  The volume button for the music was set to 12 
(out of 10) and it was difficult to hear any talking above the music.
The place looks so stark now!  It kinda looks to me like
what a living room in a hospital would look like: very institutional, if you
pretend the bar and dancefloor aren't there.  Oh well, oh well, I guess the Top
has gone through a significant change and I ain't going there no more.  :-(
No more house music, no more cozyness, no more house crowd, no more 
crowd. :-(
I do enjoy reggae though, but not at the new Top.  

Does anyone know where to spend Tuesday and Sunday nights in the house 
scene
now that the Top is gone?  I went to "rave" for Peace last Sunday night but it 
was almost empty.

- TAXI

PS. ComeUnity on Tuesday night was great: great crowd, great
atmosphere, overt friendliness, great music, it wasn't too big and it
wasn't too small.  Plus many of the people there were hard-core
ravers: nice bunch of people.

Sunday night is techno night at the Cactus Club in San Jose.

They call it NEMESIS.

I went there a couple times and found it to be pretty good (my standards are 
kinda low, though). The music was hardcore |) and there were some interesting 
people to watch. It was definitely a club atmosphere, however.

If anybody's in San Jose on a Sunday night, they should drop by. It is
free before 9:30 and cheap after that ($4 I think).

--------------------

Re: all the negative e-mail.

Seems like half the volume on this list is being spent on what shouldn't be
talked about, what shouldn't be flamed, and so on. I'd personally rather
see a bunch of interesting flames, sarcasm, off-the-wall opinions -- you
know, real-life stuff. The uptightness, politeness, and mock-love of the
happy happy joy joy love love orthodoxy gets to be a bit tiresome because
it is so artificial.

Is the sense of community there only because we're all so wrapped up inside
our heads that we're never willing to let on what is really felt and
thought? "Love peace and understanding" is not going to happen if we're all
just silent dancers -- communication, disagreement, reconciliation are all
part of understanding and love.

Also, you gotta have a sense of humor about the absurdities of life, of
others, and of self if "love peace and understanding" is to have any
meaning other than some shallow reverberation of the lost ethos of the
60's.

End of sermon. Now everybody send me $1.00 or you'll rot in hell forever.

In the past, when there have been two events being held at 1015 Folsom (Martini 
on Friday nights) on the same night and with over-lapping hours, the side door 
(in the alley) has been used for entry. When I went to a Sharon there, they kept 
us waiting in line for a long time, and when we got to the door, it cost us 10 
bucks.  Had I known that ahead of time, I'd have walked around to the front 
door and paid the same 10 bucks to go into Martini and not wait in any lines. The 
music was exactly the same (same room, same crowd, same everything). 
(Actually, now that I think of it, it was a Candyland not an official Sharon). 
Anyway, consider yourself warned, if the lines are long, then go around to the 
front. Martini closes at 4 am, so don't expect Ira to throw all the people out at 2 
am and let ravers in. The dance music room (aka The Pit) had some house, some 
techno, some rap, and some popular music. I don't know how they're gonna 
pull this one off with Garth and Jeno DJ'ing. Expe!
ct jazz in the basement.  

Martini was actaully pretty good in it's heyday (disco/funk/soul room, and The 
Pit, and Mama's downstairs (live jazz)).  But like I said, when I went to 
Candyland last year, there wasn't a separate room for the ravers to party, 
everybody mixed, and listened to the same dance music and had access to the 
same rooms, etc. So caveat emptor!

I went to ToonTown's bday.  It was my third rave, and it wasn't as much
fun as anticipated.  The macho attitude was present, and it really created
a lot of bad vibes for me.  Homophobes threw things and pushed people into
me and my boyfriend as we kissed.  I witnessed the same group persistently
propositioning this girl - continuing to kiss and "sweet-talk" her even
though she made it clear she wanted to get by them.  Also, the music was
mediocre and wasn't mixed very well.  The space was cool and the lighting
effects were fun, but it was hard to get into it (especially on the weak
stuff I was on).

For my boyfriend, it was sort of sad - he's been into the scene since last 
summer and knew ToonTown when it was hardcore.  I guess it was to be
expected, considering the heavy mainstream advertising they've been 
pushing (read: ufo's).  

Damn, should have saved that energy for Mr. Floppy's!

-Joel (the other one!)

I know this is all really basic obvious stuff, but perhaps
someone will benefit? 

The experience one has, at any place and time, is as much
created by the self as by the people around him/her. Indeed,
with raves, this is one of the most important aspects:
bringing with one a good mood and a willingness to create
for ones self and for others good feelings.  As well as what
one creates ones self, there is an amazing wonderfulness and
synergy to these feelings and more created when these
feelings of good are shared from one to another. One of the
implicit ways this is shared during raves is on the dance
floor where the floor is covered with people using it to its
fullest, and where people are intent on helping each other
feel accepted, warm, whatever; one can be euphoric in such a
place, even without chemical catalysts! 

These delightful and good feelings have as one of their
catalysts people who know all these things.  While one can
have a good time anywhere, it isn't the same as when there
are others like minded in these ways. People not knowing
these things offset the ratio.  Some of the common ways for
people not knowing these things to show up at raves are with
(overly) wide advertisement (such as big posters on every
telephone pole, mass media advertisements).  Another way I
found out recently is for a bar which uses the same place
for a  dancing event starting at 2AM after another function
just ended. 

(Bizhan, thank you for your comments, they are most true and
depicted a similar story to what happened Friday.  I wish I
had read them earlier ...) 

Learning all this, I was disappointed with Wicked ($7) and
didn't really expect anything more than what I got at
ToonTown ($10) ... and reading my own advice worked well
when I decided to think about things while dancing at around
5AM ... it's nice being submerged in the earth where one
cannot see the sun, even though it easily lights up the
surface brightly. 

I missed Gorbachev (I overslept) -- what did he say? 


btw, what does everything think Wacky Citrus will be like? 

I should find all my flyers and send them to Vitamin B, but
I'm sort of burning out on the task (it's a lot of paperwork
and effort to collect all these flyers!)  One interesting
one is worth mentioning: 

Rave for Peace, Golden Gate Park @ The Band Shell
Free for all, Saturday May 16, 11am-6pm

(Don't forget there should be a full moon rave sometime
around the 16th, as well as an unknown time & point for High
Summit (on Hamilton), as well as Wacky....) 

Of course, that's the same day as a zillion other raves and
events. Suggestions, anyone? 

See everyone around!

Brad / Ulmo

I apologize for having to do this, but I am unfortunately the one
who has to kick the mailing list off of our site.  Why?
We are a cluster of Apollo SINGLE-USER workstations, yet
we have just about 4,000 accounts.  This makes for a SLOW cluster,
and for a cluster which is prone to crashing.

We have one machine partially dedicated to mail, and that goes down
just when we have normal mail, let alone mail to mailing lists
with over 150 people.

Thus, in order to provide the maximum service to our local users,
we can no longer afford to provide the mailing list service
to this mailing list.

I apologize for the inconvenience.  I understand that Mr. Behlendorf
has arranged for the mailing list to be moved... For a short while,
you will still be able to send mail to this site until you get
used to the other site -- we will provide a pointer upstairs to 
the machine on which the mailing list will hopefully find a 
(semi)permanent home.

Thanks for understanding,

Dave Friedman
Postmaster
Open Computing Facility
University of California at Berkeley
postmaster@ocf.Berkeley.EDU
postmaster@UCBOCF.BITNET

I'm finnaly gonna take the stand and defend alcohol.  It's not one of
my favorite drugs either, and I don't take it that often but when I 
want to take some drug, be it asprin or opium, I'll do it regardless
of if it's "pc" or not.  I think real ravers know how to take there
drugs.  A little alcohol is not so horrible.  The problem most people
seem to have with it is the way it makes people belligerent which is
NOT condusive to the rave atmosphere/message/culture BUT the kind of
people who drink to that point or get like that are the kind of people
we all are always complaining about and who shouldn't be at raves anyway.
Actualy, maybe they should and hopefully they'll catch on to what's up.
I think the underground raves needn't wory about alcohol because it 
doesn't seem to cause a problem.  Raves like Toon Town, etc. should
get rid of their dumb bars as far as I'm concerned.  That would be the
best thing Toon Town could do in my opinion.

p.s. This message is a reponse to ovid's message but it's not pointed that
     way.  It was kinda like the straw that broke the camels back.|-)

-Mark

Short report on Wicked-
Good (not great) small rave in the basement at 1015 Folsom (I think) on 
Sat. night.  Had it's ups and downs but the downs weren't realy down, just
DJ or dancefloor lulls.  Met some good people.  I felt a community atmosphere
and was at the giving and receiving end of sharing at different points 
throughout the evening (morning).  Noticed deadheads who came from the 
Jerry
show at the Warfield and danced all night.  Good people, same ideals and 
energy.Didn't see any sfraves buttons but did notice and converse with Taxi, who 
is
always noticeable with his blue and white striped elf's hat.  One mildly
amusing story:  My friend steve and I accidentaly paid and got into 
"Martini" which was going on at ground level.  We couldn't figure it out
for the longest time why things weren't "right".  Finnaly, while searching
for wicked without even realizing it, I stumbled outside and was asked by
and eager bunch "is that the door to the underground rave?".  I instantly
figured it out, went back inside, grabbed a (usualy) clueless Steve, and
proceeded to the correct door.  At this point we had $3 between us but
we had rode on my motorcycle from the Berkeley at 2 in the morning and 
paid the right club for the wrong event and we were determined to get in.
After explaining our embarrasing story to consecutive levels of the
management hierarchy, a really cool guy named Luke (I think) said in a 
fatherly tone "Come on in guys, and let's get the right one next time, heh?"
Anyway, so much for my "short" report.
-Mark

	To paraphrase LFO, the SFRAVES LIST IS BACK.

	This new machine, soda, will hopefully be much more capable of
sustaining the list. It took a bit of begging, so be kind to the list
you all... no flame wars, please! Thank you for your patience over the
past week - while some people have expressed their confusion and discontent
by unsubscribing, most of you were kind enough to just keep deleting the
errant messages. 
	I've processed all the new requests, as well as all the unsubscribe
requests, but I may have missed one or two - so if you still want off, even
now with the promise of a cleaner list, let me know. 

	To set it all straight - all posts should now go to sfraves@SODA.
berkeley.edu, all list requests to sfraves-request@soda, and all mail to
me to owner-sfraves@soda. I'll let the other relevant mailing lists and
newsgroups know, too. I hate this instability, but I think this is the 
end of it.

	As a bonus for your patience, I'm including with the post the updated
calendar, as well as a post andrea sent me about public-access unix accounts
for anyone out there who will be losing their school account in the next month.
(Oh yeah, a reminder - mail me if you're losing your account soon.)

	Phew..... now I'm off to study for finals (yeah right)

	Brian

>	To paraphrase LFO, the SFRAVES LIST IS BACK.

yahoo!  thanks for the perserverence and dedication to the rave
ideal above and beyond the call of duty, brian.  in the history of the
net, you will go down as a saint among list managers.

anyway, enough butt kissing.  to celebrate the return of sfraves, i'll
tell you all about brainstorm this weekend...

in a word, it sucked.  well, it wasn't really THAT bad, but it was
very non-rave-like.  it took place at the jack london club (aka The
Flophouse) in oakland, which i had never been to.  an interesting
space, to be sure - lots of twisty hallways and small rooms.  the main
dance floor is rather small but it was not crowded.  the sound system
was adequate but not particularly good - it gave me a whanging
headache every time i went near it, in fact.  contrast this to the
sound system at townsend, which was about a billion times louder but
not at all painful.  other items of interest were:

* a chill room with a layer of grass on the floor - fun for lounging
around in, and it smelled a lot better than the stale sweat aroma of
the dance floor

* a room done up to look like some sort of abbattoir - it was
obviously some kind of art statement, and fairly neat for that

* a room with a large TV running some sort of "new cinema" showcase

* a neato device with a tv camera and a screen.  you push a button and
it adds the picture on the screen to all the other images it has
stored up.  on the other side of the box is a different screen running
through all the stored images at a very high speed.  incredibly trippy
device!  (it was called the "imagebase")

* cool reggae band playing when we got there

despite all these attractions, the rave never really jelled.  a
certain indefinable "x-factor" was missing.  not a lot of positivity
from the crowd, i guess.  it was just sort of a
more-interesting-than-usual trip party, i guess.  oh well.

Jon Drukman (finely honed machine)              uunet!sco!jondr   jondr@sco.com
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Homing in on the inner sanctum of the out-take.

OK folks,
	Here your chance to give some much needed feedback for
a worthy cause.

A couple of friends and I are trying to organize a "rave-type" event
for the end of July.  (It's a rave-type event cause it only goes from
like 6pm till midnight)

We tentitively are calling it ECO-RAVE.  It would be a fund raiser for two
non-profit organizations
			1) eco-rap
			2) battered womens' shelter

Eco-rap is an organization that promotes and encourages ecological
awarness and action in innercity areas.  


The tentitive dates are July 25 a saturday or July 26, a sunday

We can rent an area at the fort mason center with a capacity of about
300 - 400 This area divides nicely into three spaces so we can have
two simultaneous DJ's and a chill-out room.

We'd like to get a couple of "big name" DJs like SPUN Ernie DIG-IT , etc.
to do it pro-bono or at a reduced cost and would also be spinning
reggae, rap and world-beat in the smaller room and techno-rave in the
big room.

Unfortunately, we cannot go longer than midnight - this is flat.

Now for the market research (This is where you come in!)

---------------------- cut here ----------------------------------------------

1) Would think about attending such an event? [y/n]
2) Would you bring your friends? [y/n]
3) Would you tell your friends? [y/n]
4) Which day is better ? [sat. /sun.]
5) How much should we charge? [ <$5, $5, $10, >$10]
6) How importent is a killer light show? [zilch,important, absolutely]
7) How important is it to have "Big name DJs"? [zilch,important, absolutely]
8) Would you bring your mother to this event?[y/n]
9) Do you think we will make any money? [y/n]
10) Is this a good "first rave" event for a non-raver? [y/n]

    "big" rave is happening on the same night? (remember we're
    thru at midnight.) [y/n]
12) Do you think people will come on a Sunday night, if they have to
    go to work on monday?

I sent mail yesterday informing everyone on the list that Inside Edition was
going to have a segment on raves Tuesday night, but the sfraves was not up
yet. Well if you didn't see it, here are some (negative) excerpts:
 
1) An ex-Raver was interviewed and he said there were a lot of sex going
   around.  He said he saw people having sex in dark hallways and in one
    rave, they were doing it on the dancefloor! They said it was caused
    by X.
2) They said there are nudity in the raves.  They had a hidden video camera
   showing a naked girl with wings, dancing. This is my type of rave ;-)  
3) They said mostly everyone is on X or laughing gas: 
    They were harrassing this quy because he kept saying x to everyone.
4) They said rave is very dangerous because two guys died from laughing
   gas. They assumed they were ravers because they had rave flyers in
   truck that they died in.

The raves on the show were from SoCal. 

Inside Edition really wanted to tell all the moms on what their kids are
doing at the raves.  At the end, the host was just nodding his head.

Back in the late summer of 1990, I accidentally videotaped this segment of
Inside Edition on raves. It was a total no-information thang, but fairly
benign. On top of that, they weren't even spreading any cool
disinformation, such as the nude winged angel and sex on the dancefloor.
What drugs were the TV-folk on when they saw all that? Maybe they were in
some suggestible state while the DJ was playing DAF's "Voulez Vous Coucher
Avec Moi" from Twitch #1? (note plug! -- can I get CD03 yet?)

Well, you know they won't be Inside Editioning the alchohol-inspired public
nudity that goes gland-in-hand wth the New Orleans Mardi Gras.  A common
occurance at that event is for ogreous beer-swilling southern men riding on
the floats to yell out "show yer tits" to women watching the parade. Women
who submit to their lecherous will (or fling their undergarments back) will
get thrown extra-special suuuper doooper mardi-gras beads. Feminism :-) has
crept into the scene of late because the women sometimes shout "Show yer
dick!" -- and in the gay quarter, they'll show the length and breast of it!

Shocking? Only in good-ol-protestant indoctrinated amerikkka! 

Just by way of further rambling, the reason why I recorded that
inside-edition segment is cuz I wanted to get some sound-bytes from this
reportage of the police department's use of pot-bellied-pigs as
drug-sniffing dogs. Totally stuuuupid! That segment, and the natl'
geographic segment on the sex lives of bats will definitely make for some
cool quoted-out-of-context "lyrics" in some upcoming techno/industrial
song.

"He envelops her with his bat-perfume!"
"The singer with the best voice will be chosen to sire the next generation"
etc.

>	Yup, we all got reamed by the Santa Clara PD last night. RAVE for PEACE

Yeah, we sort of had a little post-midnight "rave diaspora".  Except this
time, instead of having our temple burned and being chased out of the Land
by the roman opressors and ending up all over the world, we had our party
broken up and we were chased out of the house by the Santa Clara PD, ending
up all over Northern California.  Oh well.  We still have our Zionist dream
of getting together and raving 'til the full moon is replaced by the morning
sun.

Well, one group of us went to the beach at La Honda.  Not many people, but
it was so beautiful.  The sky was very cloudy and so the moon didn't come
through, printing the world a four-ink grey.  It was calming and focusing.
An excellent way to wait for the sun to rise.

ahh, what the heck, here it is ...

e info - practical information about ecstasy

* The multifaceted jewel *
Ecstasy catalyzes a powerful experience that takes many different
forms.  It can provoke an intense, energetic, spiritual high or lead
to warm, loving relaxation.  It can connect people freely and openly
with each other or promote deep inner thinking and analysis.  Sensual
yet not necessarily sexual, beautiful and sometimes dangerous, Ecstasy
covers a wide range of human emotions, experiences, and passions.
What you put into it is what you get out, so be sure to explore the
many facets of the experience.

* Those little annoying side effects *
Although some people say it has no side effects, Ecstasy is not the
perfect drug.  Users have reported a variety of mild physical symptoms
such as jaw clenching, teeth grinding, eye wiggles, tightened muscles,
sweating, chills, increased heart rate, blood pressure and body
temperature, auditory effects, nausea, shaking, and next-day
sleepiness.  Occasionally it can cause toxic reactions in people with
asthma, heart conditions, diabetes, epilepsy, psychosis, or
depression.  Remember, Ecstasy is a power drug.  Treat it -- and your
body -- with respect.

* As time passes ... *
Myths abound concerning Ecstasy's effects after repeated usage.  Most
claims (such as that it causes Parkinson's disease or drains spinal
fluid) actually refer to other drugs or common misconceptions.
Although scientists suspect some nerve terminal damage and
neurotransmitter depletion in the brain based on animal research, the
true long term effects and implications remain a mystery until further
human research becomes legal.  By avoiding the temptation to use
Ecstasy too frequently, you can lessen the risk and have more fun.

* Less is more *
An active dose of Ecstasy depends on one's body weight, sensitivity,
and prior use.  A typical "hit" contains 75-125 milligrams.  Over 175
milligrams increase side effects for many users.  Taking a larger dose
does not necessarily mean a better experience -- it may be more
"speedy," but less ecstatic.

Remember to integrate what you've learned.  Think about your thoughts
and feelings and try to apply them to real life.  No masterpiece was
created in a day; leave time to reflect on your experiences, and you
will have an even stronger base to build on.

* Methylenedi-what?? *
The chemical name for Ecstasy is "methylenedioxymethamphetamine," or
MDMA for short.  It is created in laboratories through an elaborate
scientific process.  First patented in 1914 by the Merck Co. of
Germany, its human use only goes back to the early 1970s, when it was
used recreationally and therapeutically.

Therapists found MDMA helped people to bring out their true feelings
in a peaceful and open manner, and they used it that way, quite
legally, for many years.  In the mid-80s it exploded into the
nightclub scene in Texas, and was promptly banned.

* What the government did *
In 1985, MDMA was declared illegal in the United States.  Despite the
objections of scientists, doctors, and even judges, it was placed
along with marijuana, LSD and heroin on Schedule I, a classification
of drugs with no recognized medical use and high abuse potential.
Although therapeutic use is no longer legal, it continues to be used
recreationally and socially.

* Be an informed shopper *
Useful facts about drugs can be hard to find among the anti-drug hype.
Here are some excellent books worth reading.  Try asking your local
bookstore to order them:

  `Ecstasy: The MDMA Story' by Bruce Eisner (Ronin Press)
  `PIHKAL: A Chemical Love Story' by Ann & Alexander Shulgin
     (Transform Press)
  `Pursuit of Ecstasy: The MDMA Experience' by Jerome Beck & Marsha
     Rosenbaum (forthcoming from SUNY Press later this year)

`Xochi Speaks', a full-color educational poster and booklet, provides
practical info on chemistry, dosages, effects, side effects, etc. of
MDMA and eleven other psychedelic substances, as well as general facts
about brain chemistry, nutrition, and the psychedelic experience.
Send a stamped, self-addressed envelope to Lord Nose!, P.O. Box
170473R, San Francisco, CA 94117.

The Multidisciplinary Association for Psychedelic Studies (MAPS) funds
scientific research on MDMA and has publications available about MDMA
and other psychedelic drugs.  Write to MAPS, 1801 Tippah Ave.,
Charlotte, NC 28205; (704) 358-9830.

v back page v

[ a chemical diagram, it's pretty and decorative, I wonder it
actually is something ]

Ecstasy and the rave scene combine to form a positive human energy; it
can bring people together and promote peace, love and understanding.

We hope this flyer helps provide useful information and removes some
of the mysteries.  Please be careful and responsible; learn from your
experiences here.  Take the joy and spirit of these experiences home
with you, and together, we can make this a better world for everyone.

The publishers and distributors of this flyer do not condone or
encourage drug use.  It's none of our business if you use drugs or
not, but if you do, be careful.  Keep the scene alive for all of us,
and remember:  drink lots of water.

				e info

Look for more from info-e at future raves.

[typed in directly from yellow flyer handed out at GG rave '92my16sa]

Well I GOT IN!!!
And stayed till about 8 am and it was great!!

I arrived at about midnight, I parked my car along the side of 
glenview and started to walk the 1/4 mile or so to the house.
I had a flash light so I could see where I was going.  Eventually
three crusiers passed by me.  They got on the loud speaker and said
stuff like "The party's over kids, go home", etc.  I knew from previous
experience with the police that this is a typical tactic, but I also
know that you cannot win against cops with brut force unless you
GREATLY out number them but you can use the powers of the mind.  So I just 
walked right past them, my friends must have been to timid to follow cause
I climbed up to the hill to find the party IN FULL EFFECT, people were
goin' off all over the place.  I was have so much fun that I forgot about my
friends at the front of the road, so I went back down to get them and also
something I left behind.  Well I didn't see my friends so I went back up the hill 
only to be stopped by a cop saying that I couldn't go in, but I thought
fast so here's this big macho cop tellin me I can't go in, I may be big
but he's got a club and a gun and several other buddies who had the same.
So I say in my best "air head California accent, "Hey Officer, my girlfriend is
still in there with all those horny guys comon man gimme a break, I can't leave
her in there!"... and IT WORKED!! He said well, you look trust worthy,
you go get her and come back out ya hear!  "You bet Office ! Sure thing!"

So I got past the first Cop and was challenged as I went up the hill but
I just told then the sargent at the botton of the hill let me through, after the third 
cop they didn't bother me any more so I just went the rest of
the way and told other folks to beware if they tried to leave.

The party was still jumping, this was a BIG house situated on a hill
in a redwood grove.  There was a pool in the basement a chill-out area, in the
basement, and everyone was dancing outside near the garage.  After about 1/2
hour, the music stopped outside, I guess this was due to neighbor complaints.
But someone put music on inside the house and the party continued.  Some 
people
left other went down the hill to the back yard to sit around a HUGE firepit
with burning logs in it and just chill out.  There seemed to be a plentyfull
supply of X judging from the behavior of several people that I saw. After
about an hour , we cranked up the music again with the speakers moved to 
inside
the garage.  I don't know who was spinning but it kept getting better and 
better (with a few bad spots here and there). All in all, I had fun, I left
at 8 am.  I dove a few people to the City and crashed at a friend's house
for a few hours, waking up just in time for Rave for Peace.

I went to Wacky Citrus on Saturday. I had been looking
forward to it for a long time, because the flyer was so
pretty. Here are my itemized opinions:

+ Excellent light show! The lasers and lights of color
  were the best I have ever seen. They had a four color
  laser, a red laser, and a green laser. Sometimes the 
  lasers would just scribble all over the walls and ceiling
  and it was like a very intense acid trip.

+ Good music. Ernie Munsen (or whatever) was spinning some
  incredible energy, and some people and I had to scream
  to release all the pressure that we couldn't get out
  by dancing fast enough. I think some guy named Blow
  played muted trumpet, and it was a truly beautiful sound
  backed by the pounding techno foundation.

- Environment. It was in the Fashion Center, and there
  was only the one big dance floor, nothing else. I
  didn't really enjoy paying $20 for it, but oh well.

- The people. There were some real ravers there, and 
  they were the ones who kept me going. However, most
  of the people seemed kinda clubbish, and I didn't get
  that feeling of community on the dance floor that you
  get at truly great raves.

Did anybody else go and have different impressions?

How about a real illegal rave at Fort Funston.  If you haven't been there,
they have tunnels and old military bunkers that was used for cannons. It's
really dark inside but when there's a full moon and no fog, the light will
shine thru the cannon openings overlooking the ocean. Also, it's sound
proof. :-)  There's also this place near Daly City, near Westmoor H.S.
The left front is a playground and the right side is a Mormon Church, but in
between there's this gate that leads to a cliff overlooking the Pacific
Ocean.  There's a path the goes about a mile downwards thru trees and bushes 
and ends up at an isolated beach.
The only problem is that the equipment has to be parachuted down the cliff.;-)


don - "Listen to the Rhythm Flow" ~~~~~~^v^v^v^v^v

It was truly funny to see all of the really drugged out dazed people
walk up the stairs and say "oh  my god it's sunny outside" very
annoyed at the sun.  I had much more fun at Sharon (until about 5am
when someone annoyed me and I left for the remains of Care*Free to
regain my psyche -- which didn't get regained until I went to I slept
last night, Really!; that big TV in ToonTown has got to go -- well,
perhaps, it was pretty trippy with psychedelic seens and a dancer in
front, nahh, too tvish). End Up was interesting -- awake people
talking happily and from all over, actually the vibes were bad at best
but somehow it was the right atmosphere for me to regain myself. 

Weary tired me (happier and more jovial about things) walked to Market to
get wahtever bus rumbled my way, and promptly got on an N (strange to get
on an N when the sun is shining bright!).  The N got stuck without a way
to get back to where it needed to go, and I had to cross all these crazed
runners just to get home.  I'm glad the band playing two blocks from my
house wasn't any closer; their musical selections could have been better ...
That's the thing.  Running doesn't fit the rave scene, I decided, and
slept quite well.

All in all a great weekend, my fun mostly at Golden Gate,
and I would have had a fun as hell time Friday if I had simply stepped aside
when the cops left (I should have!  Argh ...)

  The mere trickle of mail bouncing in from the Rave list tells me that folks
are busy raving over finals etc. right now. So, just to keep the flow going:
  Last Sunday there was a "rave" in GG Park held in the music concourse. Decent
DJing, about 50+ people dancing when I got there. General good vibes and a 60s
feeling. It was fun to notice that sometimes the dancing would kind of droop
down to a perfunctory level; then suddenly awhomping bass line or thunderous
drum would come powering in, and you could *visibly* notice the energy level 
of
the dancing go up.
  I wore my SFR pin (thanx, Brian!) and it served as an intro to two other
netters. If you/we go raving this summer, be sure to stick on that button. It
makes for instant camaraderie -- nice if you're out solo at a rave.
  Ace those finals! "To rave is to affirm!"

	About making one of these the next location for our picnic - sounds
great! But how could we still have food/etc? What about something that starts
around 5 or 6 PM, and then we have food and get hyped up until sundown, at
which time we start bouncing like mad, finishing around 1 or 2 to go on
to the night's festivities. Or maybe we could think of something very
counter-culturish to do for three hours, and then make that a general-
admission event lasting until dawn....

	Re: Urb. Yes, it's a LA Club rag, actually not a bad magazine but
one of the elements most responsible for making the LA Rave scene as over
the top as its become. When you can pick the mag up at Music Plus or the
Wherehouse (which many LA outlets of those chains stock for free), what's
so underground about it? Ooops there goes my snobbiness again. They also
have many articles about the music, which is a plus in my mind, as well as
article about rap and acid jazz, which is also good. The articles could be
better written, but they're often very interesting. I have one with an
interview with Doc Martin in which he envisions weekend-long raves in the
desert with 20,000 people (what, doesn't he think LA youth have JOBS?
SCHOOL? :) Anyway, pick it up if you can.

	Coming soon... a current calendar, as well as my view of the
weekend's activities. My finals are OVER WITH!!! YEAH!!!

>I'm most drawn to the idea of having it on private property [less red  tape
>than state parks] with very good logistical planning WRT parking and 
carpooli>[and bathrooms].           from M Normal

Seems like the ideal to me.  I've been checking for places around
Santa Cruz for awhile.  Good alnight beaches with adequate secure 
parking and space for hundreds are rare.  Vast meadows near the
coast, nestled among the mountains and/or redwoods, seem best.
Private, consenting poperty, with acres and attendants for parking,
trash cans and recycling bins, organic foods, juices, and 
smart products for sale at reasonable prices, and clusters of
Port-o-potties near the woods.  (With 'Beware of poison ivy' signs).
*All day Saturday (4th of July -- Rube Goldberg's birthday?!),  :-)
Saturday night, *and* Sunday, or even the weekend of June 13.
The summer solstice weekend (June 20 & 21) already has a few things
in the works.  We could start this thing over where Altamont left off
in '69.  This IS the 25th anniversary of The Summer of Love ('67-'92),
though many are already calling it The Summer of Raves.  Should be hot!



>I don't know about Bolinas.  They are the closest thing around to an
>intentional community, and might perceive it as an invasion [which it might
>in fact be, considering how many people tend to show up].

Bolinas is having a hard time turning away the hordes now.
Most of the townspeople weren't happy about the CNN press, etc.
they got last year.  It's one of my very sacred, special spots
in the universe to take a special friend.  (please don't quote me
on that;-)  Can't imagine what would happen if hordes of ravers
descended on them.  There are, perhaps, spots around Larkspur, or
perhaps the Lucas Ranch...    :-)

Greetings earthlings!
	I too deeply regretted the $20 I spent on Wacky Citrus.  I think the 
crowd was overwhelmingly composed of drunken jostlers.  In addition, I do not 
think that the 'wall of sound' idea came off too well.  Perhaps, if you were 
close up front it was okay, but from where I was dancing there was terrific/
horrific base reverberations.  Now, despite the regrets, Ernie and Scott 
did justice to some fonkee beats that still drove me to dance all night long.
I saw quite a few friendly faces (I WAS wearing my SFR button this time!), and
I was coming from a pre-Citrus Rave warmup held in Davis.  So, I had a great 
time anyway.  
	If anyone went to DNA afterwards, this was really the place to be!  I 
think it was Robbie Hardkiss spinning(please forgive & correct me if I am 
backwards on these names!).  The floor was smoking with the happiest, 
energetic,
ravers from the night before.  The music energized me from 7 until 11 at which 
time our happy caravan trekked to Golden Gate Park.  WOW!!!  I'll let someone 
else describe it from here.

	Just one more thing.  Is it me or does everybody tend to have a great 
time no matter what?  On second thought, don't answer that...

VooDoo Chile

From: mcg@netcom.com (Mykl G)

Subject: Resurrection
Status: R

At the end of a rather bumpy weekend (being intimidated away from the
FMR, enjoying a fabulous Rave for Peace, getting totally Wacky with
Citrus), the new club Resurrection at DNA Lounge Sunday morning was an
excellent spot to glide back to earth.  More spacious and less insane
than Zanzibar, the huge black-light art pieces made for one of the
best indoor ambiences I've experienced lately, and the DJ work by
Robbie Hardkiss and guests was inspired and inspiring.  Although
not particularly crowded (maybe 50 people in all) there was lots
of eye-contact, community feeling, what-have-you.  A high degree of
interaction between dancers.  The balcony upstairs makes for a good
chill space with a bird's eye view of the floor.

- MykL G

I know there's a lot of skepticism about Bolinas as a possible rave site
because of their reputation for xenophobia.  On the other hand, the town
also has very heavy 60's counterculture vibes, and might be receptive to
what rave culture has to offer.  The only way of resolving this would be
to find some actual Bolinas residents (possibly friends of someone on this
list) and run the idea past them.  I know it's a slim chance, but the
possibility of it working out is intriguing.

- MykL G

was the night for "the delirium incident". Here's what I saw:

language nazis)...  music was basically disco (e.g.  clinton's atomic dog),
rap (how i could just kill a man by cypress hill, plus some cuts offa Tribe
Called Quest "low end theory"), etc. DJ was "Amy Tran" (i think... this is
all from memory).

The bad news is that if you're looking for a rave, thursday's at townsend
ain't it -- basically, a complete mix of humans, ranging from B-boys and
youngish gangsta-lookin' dudes, to "house music" types, down to your
average club type folk dressed in nice clothes.

But for $5.00 w/ free drinks, it was a reasonable way of spending a few
hours.

Not that I am one to condone drug use in any way, shape or form, but I
thought I'd put forth a small but significant addendum to those that are so
inclined -- BEWARE!!

I've seen numerous reports indicating that Prozac is quite unsafe -- I
believe investigations are underway that may get it banned by the FDA, even
for prescription use.

Basically, what happens is that some people that take it undergo a complete
personality change, including episodes of violence sometimes leading up to
murder.  I recall hearing something about 50 lawsuits pending where prozac
has been indicated in causing people to go completely ape-shit!

So, as they say caveat emptor, cave canem, et pro bono puella est pulcher...

			--------------------

>she handed me a photo of two hands with flyer information painted on them.
>Basically, at the old Underground on Thursday nights, Scott n' Robbie Hardkiss
>will be doing a weekly (?) wave.

This is true - Scott gave me this flyer himself :). I forgot to put it on the
list in the weekly section... anyway, it's called "Deep Faith", Thursdays at
210 9th Street, with the Hardkiss Bros, and "future guest spots" - Jeno,
Garth, Bones, Ernie Munson, Noel & many more. Finally something cool on
Thursday nights... what do other people know about the location?


Also, I wanted to say I had a ton of fun at Sharon on Saturday. True, I wished
it were at a more "underground" location than Big Heart City, but the layout
isn't bad there. I LOVED the computer animation/video art they had going on
a couple of TV's. And to he who said the music wasn't par, I must contest.
Spun was doing a great job mixing, had an excellent selection of music (what
was that song, Mike, Alien Encounters or something?). That was also the second
time I've heard him play Meat Beat Manifesto's Helter Skelter, which sounded
GREAT. *** I'm sure I annoyed a lot of people with my "found art" collection
that night, the traffic beacon hanging from my neck and the small flashlight
I kept shining around, my "intellabeam in a palm". The sound system was 
amazingly clean, too - I think the layout with 4 satellite speakers doing themids
and the highs, and two huge bass cabinets, works incredibly well. As for the
atmosphere... there were a lot of sfravers there, which made it very fun, and
many of the people there were easygoing and friendly, but the lighting man did
have the lights on too much for my taste. There was also this bizarre mating 
ritual going on in the middle of the dance floor around 5 or 6, between this 
scantily clad 5' female and a bare-chested 6'2" male, which at times came close
to what one could call techno-lambada... didn't seem to fit, anyways. It was
heartening to know that around 6:30, of the dozen or so hard-core dancers on
the floor, us sfravers comprised about half :)

	See ya at the Delirium Incident (maybe)...

	Brian

p.s. - anybody with an academic account who knows they're going to lose it
soon, either send me mail asking to unsubscribe or tell me when you need me
to take you off.

Hi Kids!

I feel like it's been forever since I went out dancing, so I'm off to Housing
Project tonight @ the endup!  I'm bummed that I was out of town for the
weekend, but I'm back and a-rarin' to go.  (Ever had a mudbath -- I was all set
to go out dancing after my first mudbath this weekend, but, alas, no raves in
Calistoga!)  There were a few messages I wanted to respond to, so here goes...

A. is for apple

Giamma:  I lovEd your mEssagE!  Reading it right after Brian's review of
Sharon, I had an idea.  Brian sounded like he had a great time.  And other
people thought it was lame.  One of the things that affects your perception of
a rave is your state of mind, whether your state is chemically altered
or whether you're just in a good mood, and "high on life."   Either way, it
might be interesting for reviews of raves to include reviews of the reviewer,
because the first thing I think when I read two differering reviews of a rave
is "OK, were you on X?"

Like, maybe:  "I had the *time-of-my-life*!  I've never seen such a high
energy level!  Of course, I was on 16 hits of X, 10 hits of acid, and about 40
minithins..."

Or:  "Being in a good mood, I had lots of fun dancing and connecting with
people on the dance floor."

Or:  "It was awful, but then I realized I was in a shitty mood and no wonder
I'm not having a good time..."

Just an idea.  Not that it sounded like Brian was on X, or anything!  :-)

B. is for Bambam (as in "...and Pebbles")

Someone asked about 210 9th St., where the Underground used to be, regarding
Deep Faith on Thursdays.  A gay leather bar (called Cocktails) opened when the
Underground closed at 201 9th St.  It could be the same place, but I'm not
sure, never having been to the Underground, or Cocktails.

The only other recent Thursday night things I've been to are Osmosis (good
after 1:30 or 2:00) and Terriculous (The End Up, another one coming on 5/28 --
the fist one was fun even with the curfew).  Has anyone been to Freesia?

C. is for candy

Niels:  The alcohol thing -- even though I rag on those drunken straight
fraternity boy things who aren't into this rave concept, alcohol is still a fun
drug.  Nothing like getting buzzed with a few drinks and bouncing around the
dance floor.  Whee!  Quartknee once explained to me that X is a mind-expanding
drug and that alcohol was a mind-closing drug.  I concur.  Expanding on the
concept, pot would be mind-focusing and acid mind-sensitizing?  Nitrous
mind-reverberating and ethyl ether mind-blurring?  It's just a matter of
choosing a drug for the evening.  Should I have red wine or white?  It's only
when another person's choice of drug affects my experience at a rave in a
negative way that I start to get peeved.

D. is for dalmations -- 101 of them

Where's everyone going this weekend?  We have a full slate of offerings. 
Anyone want to try to meet up at any of them?  Actually after looking back at
the list(s), I take that back!  Everything seems to be going on in LA!  Bummer.
Is Immersion just going to be 8.0 with a different name?

I hope this wasn't too long and rambling for y'all!

Share and enjoy,

Tim

	Not that I like to add to the bandwidth here, but Tim brings up
a very perceptive point:

>Just an idea. Not that it sounded like Brian was on X or anything! :-)

Actually, I did have a small amount of a particular substance, far less than
I would estimate that most people at raves who do stuff take (It wasn't X
or LSD), and all it gave me was tremendous energy and a slight dizzy
feeling. The stuff I mentioned in my review were things I had hoped would
not be affected by my physical state, things like I thought the music _was_
good, that there was too much light, but that the layout of the place was
pretty cool. I don't think any of those would be influenced by the fact that
I could run up the stairs without even raising my heart rate or even beginning
to sweat. I certainly wasn't hallucinating all the other sfravers there. :)
Oh, I forgot to mention last time that there was a lot of fog provided by a
fog machine above the dance floor without an off button. I thought it was
cool - it adds to the experience, definitely, and I that was the first
effective fog machine I've seen at a rave up here...
	Anyway, Tim's point is great. Remember, you do get out of a rave
(to a certain extent) what you put into it. If you curl up into a ball in the
corner, poeple aren't going to be as friendly as if you dance, walk around,
smile, etc. On the other hand, I think we've all been to a rave that could
be in no uncertain terms called BAD (Lunacy comes to mind...)

	Brian

sayeth niels:
>I've seen numerous reports indicating that Prozac is quite unsafe -- I
>believe investigations are underway that may get it banned by the FDA, even
>for prescription use.
>
>Basically, what happens is that some people that take it undergo a complete
>personality change, including episodes of violence sometimes leading up to
>murder.  I recall hearing something about 50 lawsuits pending where prozac
>has been indicated in causing people to go completely ape-shit!

most of these charges have been filed by the Church Of Scientology
which has a vested interest in seeing Prozac banned.  the major
problem with these charges is that the Prozac was being administered
to suicidal and/or violent psychotic types to cure them of their
anti-social tendencies in the first place!  So, hardly surprising that
if it didn't work, these already-sick people would continue along
their previous lines.

i probably wouldn't go around `experimenting' with Prozac anyway.
just like i wouldn't use thorazine to get off an LSD trip...

as for the rest of the Rat Investigation - dead brilliant!  i propose
we adopt Algernon IX as the official SF Raves Mascot.

sayeth tim hyland:
>The alcohol thing -- even though I rag on those drunken straight
>fraternity boy things who aren't into this rave concept, alcohol is
>still a fun drug.  Nothing like getting buzzed with a few drinks and
>bouncing around the dance floor.  Whee!

I agree.  Very few drinkers stop at just a light buzz though, they
usually seem compelled to go on.  I went to FX once when Rick Preston
was spinning, had a beer or two and hit that floor.  It was amazing.
My only regret is that they made him play Modern Rock shit too soon.
Emptied the floor like that.  Of course, that's what club owners like
to see...

>Expanding on the concept, pot would be mind-focusing and acid
>mind-sensitizing?

i don't know that i'd call pot mind-focusing.  while it is easier to
focus on some things, it takes an awful lot of effort to do it!  i
particularly like mixing music after having a joint - it's real easy
to set the proper levels.  acid is just plain old mind-expanding in
every sense of the word.

sayeth Vitamin B:
>Oh, I forgot to mention last time that there was a lot of fog provided by a
>fog machine above the dance floor without an off button. I thought it was
>cool - it adds to the experience, definitely, and I that was the first
>effective fog machine I've seen at a rave up here...

i hate fog machines.  i didn't like it at this event.  personal
preference, i guess.  here's my Rave Review Card for last saturday's
Sharon anyway, in case anybody cares:

music: A (DJ Spun was most impressive)
lights/visuals: B- (not bad, not great - i've seen better)
space: B (small but fortunately not crowded)
crowd: B (dedicated but not as openly friendly as some i've encountered)

> This is true - Scott gave me this flyer himself :). I forgot to put it on the

> 210 9th Street, with the Hardkiss Bros, and "future guest spots" - Jeno,

> Thursday nights... what do other people know about the location?

As someone else mentioned, the former Underground is now a gay bar called
Cocktails.  On Mondays it is Krash Klub, which is that dark and scary
industrial/techno that not many on this list seem to go for.  There tends
to be an interesting blend of people there.

The bar itself has pool/pinball upstairs, and looks like a 'typical' bar.
Downstairs is another bar w/ dancefloor etc.  Not much in the way of decor;
but they'll probably bring in lasers etc.  I happen to love the place
because it brings back memories of the old Underground; your mileage may vary.

Sandra

hotter rave places in Europe soon.  There are a few house mixers

here in SF. 

If house is what you like Leige may be it.  I heard the rave scene is
dying or dead in many of the bigger cities across Europe.  But there
still is a scene in Belgium, and Berlin and some other cities.  I
heard Barcelona has real potential for an acid house explosion.

From mcg@netcom.com Fri May 22 10:15:15 1992
Received: from netcom.netcom.com by soda.berkeley.edu (5.65/KAOS-1)
	id AA22601; Fri, 22 May 92 10:04:49 -0700

From: mcg@netcom.com (Mykl G)

Subject: Sound Traffic Control
Status: R

Delirium Incident last night at 177 Townsend was definitely a "mixed
bag".  For starters, Cheb I Sabbah (half the reason I attended) played
everything *but* the Northern African / Middle Eastern dance music he's
best known for, instead spinning ambient but extremely grating noise
mixed with some bizarre vocal rantings.  The visuals, primarily distorted
video, were nightmarish in nature, reminding one more of ReSearch magazine
than the normal rave psyche-doodling.

Then "Mondo Vanilli" came on (indeed, R. U. "Ken" Sirius).  My expectations
were as low as possible for this segment, but were in fact higher than
the actual performance.  This was, if not a sick parody of multi-media
performance art, at best an extremely lame attempt at the genre, one that
would flunk a freshman course at S.F. State.  There were a couple of
dancers, one topless hugging a T.V., both splattered in fake blood, one
with something resembling a babies head in the state of half-birth.  The
"climax" of the set was a cover version of "I Am the Walrus" as Mr.
Sirius might have imagined DEVO would have done it in 1977.  I tend to
like performance art, but this was totally pointless and witless.

Fortunately, Sound Traffic Control managed to redeem the evening for me.
Warning:  I'm into "serious" electronic music and performance, and there
was a large element of that involved, but also a tribal element, with
Tim North's Hoverdrum (an instrument / sculpture consisting of a drum
set suspended from the air with lots of complex mechanical couplings,
with these couplings apparently amplified to produce strange resonances
along with the drumming), Stephen Kent's excellent Digeridoo segment
with Beth Custer on sax and Tim North again on drums, and a brilliant
finale with six drummers jamming hard (I was reminded of the Dead Can
Dance show a couple of years ago).  Also, Barry Schwartz "played" his
two extremely interesting sound sculptures, one of which resembles
an oversized turntable with the "record" being a disk of sheet metal
(some cymbal-like alloy) about ten feet in diameter, with a strange metallic
"pick-up" with a chunk of dry-ice attached.  The sounds produced were
screeching but quite rich and complex -- I'd not heard anything like it
before.  I won't try to describe his other contraption (a hybrid harp /
tesla coil?) but it was equally interesting.  On top of it all was
Naut Humon (from Rhythm and Noise) mixed, directed the image of the
sound in 3D, and adding his samples and synthesized textures.

All in all, if you're thinking this might appeal to you, check it
out yourself tonight, again at 177 Townsend.  Fortunately, Mondo
Vanilli won't be there, and Dr. Fiorella Terenzi's "Music of the
Galaxies" could only be a tremendous improvement.

The rave that followed looked and sounded promising, but after about
1/2 hour we had to call it a night.

- MykL G
