Wow.

I still haven't been to many raves, and none of them very underground
(including this one, I assume), so I was pretty impressed by The
Delirium Incident at 177 Townsend last night.  There was no problem
getting in as was feared by those who said it was a closed party or
required an invite.  Sound Traffic Control was very cool, IMHO.  They
make a bunch of cool sounds with an wide variety of sometimes very
unusual instruments (like a big metal disk and dry ice).  It's really a
spectacle.  The drum equipment was suspended in the air by bungee
cords.  The drummer just cruzed up and played in mid-air.

Mondo 2000 has some connection with this event, *and* they were giving
out free copies of issues 5 and 6 of their magazine!  I got a copy of
issue 5, and forgot to get issue 6.  They were really friendly about
giving them out (party favors).  Anyone want to pick up issue 6 for me
tonight? :-)  I guess I should be able to buy one somewhere?

Sound Traffic Control (STC) played from about 11:45 to 1.  Then DJ's
started playing some great music.  We needed to get going so we could
work the next day, but it was hard not to dance to the music.  I'm not
expert enough to classify or rate the music, I just know I really liked
it.

And, the attitude thing was really true in my case.  I was very psyched
the whole drive up from the South Bay, and had a great time throughout,
only assisted by a smart drink.  Pretty good smart drinks there too.

And now for the good news.  From the flyer I got, it looks like STC
will be there again tonight.  I guess the event called "Immersion"
tonight.  I would advise going just to see the "band" if you haven't
seen something like that before.  I'll include the info from the weekly
calendar at the end for convenience.

I saw one SFR button last night, but didn't have a chance to introduce
myself at the time, and never saw her again the rest of the night, or
any other buttons.  The button I saw was at around 10:30, before STC
started up.  So, who was it???  And, how can we get more buttons out,
or should we have some other way of identifying one another in absense
of buttons.  Like we could stand, walk, and dance around holding our
thumb and middle fingers together?

Flyers for Life Force and Creation both already in Vitamin B's list, as
well as another one or two I missed.

mikE
  ( And, I guess I'm obliged to tell you guys the title on my business card
    for my otherwise serious job: Cyberspace Interface Product Development  )

A little additional info on the dangers of Prozac, responding to this message:

>From: "Niels P. Mayer" <mayer@hplnpm.hpl.hp.com>
>
>Not that I am one to condone drug use in any way, shape or form, but I
>thought I'd put forth a small but significant addendum to those that are so
>inclined -- BEWARE!!
>
>I've seen numerous reports indicating that Prozac is quite unsafe -- I
>believe investigations are underway that may get it banned by the FDA, even
>for prescription use.

I agree with Niels Mayer that you should be extremely careful before taking
Prozac; however, the reports about Prozac being unsafe need to be put in
context.  

Millions of people take Prozac; it's currently the most popular
antidepressant.  What a lot of people find, after taking it for three to four
weeks solid, is that they feel more "invigorated" or "enlivened"; their
depression is lifted, and they feel freer to act.  Some of these depressed
people fantasized about murder but would never have acted on those feelings;
on Prozac, some seem to feel less inhibited.  In nearly all of the cases put
before the FDA, the individuals committed violent acts after being on Prozac
continuously for at least a month, which is the period of time needed to get
the antidepressant/therapeutic effect.  

I asked one doctor about Prozac, and he indicated that Prozac is relatively
safe.  He was concerned about the media's desire to ring the alarm about
Killer Drugs.  When people commit violent crimes, being on a medication can be
an easy excuse, both psychologically and legally.

That doesn't mean you should take Prozac.  I recommend that people go to their
local library and use the information to make an intelligent decision for
themselves.  (People actually learning and deciding for themselves?  My God!
What would the DEA and the FDA think???  They must hate the fact that people
are (sometimes) more difficult to control than their lab rats.)  There's an
excellent private medical library at Stanford Shopping Mall that has in its
files, along with other things, a preliminary study that found that about a
third of Stanford undergrads have at least tried ecstacy.

The alt.drugs FAQ about ecstacy is also a good source of information.  


Anyway, I look forward to seeing some of you at events this weekend...

Giamma makEs some rEally good points hErE, and so havE othErs, about
the rEsponsibility of Each ravEr to contributE to thE good vibEs of
any givEn ravE.

Still, (OK enough typographic cutEnEss!) it's possible to say that
a given event (say, Rave for Peace) is more successful than average
in the degree of positivity and interaction shown by the participants
on the whole.  And others less successful (witness Freesia last
Thursday).

That's not to say a mediocre rave can't be improved by our emitting
positivity, but odds are it will not instantly turn into a great rave.

Probably the subjective component is the most important of all.
If I find myself not in the best of spirits, tired, not succeeding
in spreading positive energy, chances are I'm going to perceive
the rave as mediocre, even if others around me are having a great
time.

As John Lennon would say, "it's all in the mind, you know!"

- MykL G

I couldn't make it until 2:30 am after dashing in from the last Grateful
Dead show at Sacramento (a good one, too).  Nothing like an eclectic
musical evening.  So I missed the aforementioned highs and lows of the
Mondo Vanilli presentation and so on.  Since I'm generally able to
observe the scene only at a distance from Portland it was an interesting
experience nonetheless.  

Things were at a good level when I came in -- good lights, massive sound,
interesting Video Toaster projections.  The dance floor was reasonably
busy most of the time with a house/techno slant to things.  I'm not real
big on the deep stuff, but it was fine for dancing.  Had to leave at 4:15
but I came away feeling quite refreshed.  The scene has evolved incredibly
since my last forays into it last fall, but I definitely came away feeling
that the regular club thing is just not all that satisfying, even at
Townsend which has plenty of space and a real low-key approach.

They said things would continue until 8 . . .

The cards I found included ones for Mystic Groove, Blow Your Head/Toontown,
Life Force and a really nice one for Creation at the Russian River next
weekend.  I'd like to try the smart cotton candy, but I'm going to be in
Las Vegas next weekend (for even more Dead shows).  Yesterday at Sacramento
they were handing out flyers for something happening at the Aladdin Hotel
next Friday night, I believe.  If I can get more info from the number
I'll post it here -- it was being billed as a rave but that seems to mean
just about anything now.

" That's not to say a mediocre rave can't be improved by our emitting
" positivity, but odds are it will not instantly turn into a great rave.

  However I must point out I notice a very direct relationship to my
participation in a dancing place and its response to me.  If I come in
to a room full of active people and sit down to stare at them, I
perceive that the activity dies down immediately from that point
onward.  If I then get up and start dancing with my own energy, my own
creativity, I perceive that the activity picks up immediately from
that point onward.
  (I have gone as far as analyzing for fakeness and weirdo factors: I
perceive that if other people may think of me as a quark, weirdo,
not-in-sync person than their actions will not follow mine as much as
try to go the opposite way; this is rare though (thank god!).)

  All this stuff is so consistent that I use it as a way to control
the mood of the floor (at least in my own eyes (see below) (what does
it really matter to me whether it's real or not?)) -- and the strange
thing is, it seems to work!
  Is it just me, or is there really a large component of control I
have over a crowd?

  I think it is a combination of the two: the impact I have on the
crowd (while wild in concept I believe a true thing) and my own
perceptions seeing more of what I'm doing than a "flat response" of
what is actually out there (uh, what's the term ...  objective, that's
it).

" Probably the subjective component is the most important of all.  If
" I find myself not in the best of spirits, tired, not succeeding in
" spreading positive energy, chances are I'm going to perceive the
" rave as mediocre, even if others around me are having a great time.

This must be it -- I read your PP here after responding to the above.
I concur.

" As John Lennon would say, "it's all in the mind, you know!"

Yes, yes, it is.

Now, what supports the mind?  That is the question.  (I know some
answers -- the mind itself; food, air & other physiological intakes
(X); physical stimuli (touch, feel, emotional things) ...)

      Not to be a dick or anything, but I see nothing underground about
raves advertised in newspapers, tickets sold at music chains, $20 ticket
prices, ravesters that go to frat formals and Grateful Boring shows.  The
Seattle scene is much smaller and is mostly illegal but we have a rave or
two every weekend and very little frat boys, hippies, jocks, or people that 
ruin the rave eXperience go to.  They are big enough that there is cool
stuff and lights, but not completely overcrowded and rarley busted by the
pigs. Usually good music too. And we almost always but the tickets at the
door, so we are not ripped off (like I here happens in California).  Well,
that is my Seattle Rave plug.  Tonight's rave is at 7th and Stacey (head
South on 6th one block past Lander and take a left). Bouncing room, smart
bar, and acid art, be there or be square.   BTW, how much does X run in
California??? Here its $15-$20 before the rave, $25-$30 a hit at the rave
(which I think is a total rip off, cause 5 or 6 years ago it was like
$6-$8 in clubs).---------------------------------dan

Well, I guess we're not in Seattle are we?

I'm sure everyone here would rather remove the commercial edge from
some of the local raves.  I know I'm one.  But I've had a good time at
the few raves I've been to so far.  I go with people I like, try and 
keep a positive attitude, enjoy what there is to enjoy, and, if I'm 
lucky, perhaps meet another person that I'll know for a long time.

Though I've just tuned into the sfravers in the last two weeks, it seems
like you people are committed to trying to keep the right kind of 
feeling alive in the rave scene.  I hope I get to meet a couple of y'all--
and if you don't mind, attend your next Full Moon Rave.  Sounds like fun.

To the future!
daniel.

pete ashdown writes that ali baba's, sam i am and gilligan's 2 were
all pathetic let-downs.  once again proving that SF is really the Rave
Capital.  although, actually, this weekend wasn't so wonderful for me
either.

first, we went to Blow Your Head at the back room of Townsend - I was
particularly psyched to hear Rick Preston and Markie Mark spinning
again.  Of course, we completely missed Rick's set - got there just as
he was leaving for the event at Big Heart City whose name totally
escapes me.  We hung out at BYH for a bit.  I wasn't impressed.
Whereas Townsend proper has an incredible floor, sound system and
lighting rig, the back room is just an empty concrete space with
dreadful acoustics.  It was too brightly lit as well - I *like* to see
who I'm dancing next to, but there is such as thing as too bright.
the visuals were pretty cool, and we helped one of the lighting guys
move his junk in so we got in for free.

after about an hour of being pummeled by the sound system and rather
incompetent DJ, we decided to check out big heart city.  it was only
$5 to get in, and the sounds and lights were much better.  BHC has a
smoke machine that they like to run near-continuously.  fortunately,
they had a laser in and it made the smoke machine useful rather than
annoying.  the crowd was small but dedicated.  we decided that we
valued being with our friends more than being at a better equipped
space, so we headed back to Blow Your Head after a little while.

we remained at BYH for the rest of the evening.  markie mark played a
(typically) phenomenal set early in the AM.  i don't know where he
gets his records from, but i want some!!  very energetic, bouncy
stuff, that seems to just get more and more intense the longer he's
spinning.  what a talent.  anyway, despite the shit sound system, we
hung out until the early morning rays shone in and showed us exactly
how grungy the whole place was.

not one of the best raves i've been to, but reasonably entertaining,
and the free admission certainly meant i got my money's worth.

Jon Drukman (finely honed machine)              uunet!sco!jondr   jondr@sco.com
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Why kill time when you can kill yourself?

One of the best things about the rave scene here is how much fun it is to go
dancing with a big group of friendly people who arent hung up on rules and
categories.  There is a feeling of tolerance and unity and fun at the best
raves.  Nobody is hung up on what the other ravers do when they're not
partying, worrying about who is a REAL raver and who is just an imposter.
I'm happy to see anyone at a rave who's never been there before if they are
there to have fun.  Including hippies, including jocks, including anybody
who isnt there to wreck things.  I'd rather party with a bunch of people
that I dont know who are there to have fun than familiar people who are
sullen and determined to find fault.  I dont think that $20 is reasonable, I
wouldnt go to a club that sells tix at BASS or Tower [unless I was on the
list :-)], but there is definitely fun to be had even at these events with
good music and a little positivity.  Lighten up, Dan, it ain't the punk
scene.  If you think hippies don't know how to party, all I can say is you
must not know any real hippies.

see you in the future...
-M

Brief review of Immersion, Friday 5-22 at 177 Townsend


Fiorella and her astral friends were A-OK by me.  What she did was
basically some new-age synth noodling over a background of ambient sounds.
These sounds were a little hard to describe; kind of mineral in nature;
swelling and falling low frequency drones with rougher, gravelly sounds on
top of them. Plus mutli-screen computer graphics, some of which were abstract
and some were pretty pictures of outer space.  It was more or less what
an 8 year old nerd would imagine an LSD experience to look adn sound like.

Sound Trafffic Control was as described by Mykl G on Thursday night exceptj
that they didn't play as long :-(   It was about the best sound quality
I've ever heard in a club.

The rave part of the night was not the most energetic.  Too many of the 
people there had come to consume art rather than to participate in a celebration.
But that's just a nuance.  The music was an execellent selection of acid and
deep house; after 4am or so I was actually hungry for techno.  Great chill
room with geological low-pitch brain-programming sounds and UV light and 
mandala-ish projections on the walls.

I guess it added up to the "Thinking Fellers' Rave".  Lots of SFR types in
attendance; glad I met you Joel and Rox!!

AstroBoy

i saw mr. theremin himself, over nintey years old, playing one at an
electronic music concert at stanford.  there are actually two anntennas,
one for volume and one for pitch.  you can get cool vibrato from them, and
do a pretty good human voice imitation.

------>  especially useless tidbit:  robert moog used to make do it yourself
theremin kits before he invented the synthesizer.

------>  buchla has invented a device that works by the same principle,
moving hands or objects aboput space, but you can map locations in 3d
space to specific midi paramaters... playing invisible instruments.
astounding capabiltity for interactive music.  i think it's called the
lightning system, and it is still extremely expensive.

rocky

>Well, the weekend wasn't a complete loss.  I did get to meet Spike Lee ;-).

So, Pete, sounds like there's a story in there...  Was he out raving?  And not
to be outdone  :^), I saw David Bowie and Iman wandering Haight Street a few
weeks ago.  It would have been cool to see them at a rave!

I went to Blow Your Head on Saturday and had a good time.  Not a great time,
but definitely a good time.  It could have had a better space, better lighting,
better acoustics, but it was a fun crowd and good music, IMHO.

But the park on Monday was by far the best Memorial Day I've ever had!  Even
better than Preston's first park rave a month ago.  Good music all around (some
of it got a bit too hard techno-ish for a sunny, happy afternoon and some of
Markie Marks disco-ish house turned me off) but all around good.  And Roger
Sanchez's set was killer!  (Roger mixes a lot of the tracks from the Strictly
Rhythm label.)

Fun crowd, some people lounging and watching; others dancing or playing 
games.
Great space -- nicely enclosed.  I was in an excellent mood and had a dozen
good friends there with me, plus the friendly sfrave faces!  I even got a date
with a cute boy named Dan!  :->

So, all in all, I had a fun weekend.  Glad I didn't go to LA.  I hope Preston
keeps this up.  Was he passing the hat to help defray the costs -- if not, next
time I'll have to search him out to help.

Share and enjoy,

Tim

better acoustics, but it was a fun crowd and good music, IMHO.

But the park on Monday was by far the best Memorial Day I've ever had!  Even
better than Preston's first park rave a month ago.  Good music all around (some
of it got a bit too hard techno-ish for a sunny, happy afternoon and some of
Markie Marks disco-ish house turned me off) but all around good.  And Roger
Sanchez's set was killer!  (Roger mixes a lot of the tracks from the Strictly
Rhythm label.)

Fun crowd, some people lounging and watching; others dancing or playing 
games.
Great space -- nicely enclosed.  I was in an excellent mood and had a dozen
good friends there with me, plus the friendly sfrave faces!  I even got a date
with a cute boy named Dan!  :->

So, all in all, I had a fun weekend.  Glad I didn't go to LA.  I hope Preston
keeps this up.  Was he passing the hat to help defray the costs -- if not, next
time I'll have to search him out to help.

Share and enjoy,

Tim

>------>  buchla has invented a device that works by the same principle,
>moving hands or objects aboput space, but you can map locations in 3d
>space to specific midi paramaters... playing invisible instruments.
>astounding capabiltity for interactive music.  i think it's called the
>lightning system, and it is still extremely expensive.

it's called the Buchla Thunder.

there was a neat program for the amiga called mandala - it took video
signal input and chromakeyed it over the image on the screen.  the
image on the screen had certain "hot spots" which triggered midi
events.  so you could paint a drawing of a drum kit on the screen,
then matte yourself over it, and whenever your hand obscured one of
the spots on the screen, it would trigger the corresponding midi
event.  now is that cool or what?

/j/

Be on the lookout for a trendy magazine called SOMA.  They are very un-rave-y,
and their latest issue has an article about the rave scene.  I only had time
to skim the article, but it didn't seem to be very broad or well-researched,
and the author definitely wasn't very positive about the whole thing.  (The
secondary title of the article was something like "Smart drinks and acid house:
Just how smart are they?")

They interviewed a few promoters and ravers.  One of the quotes tickled my
fancy a whole bunch: "There's no substance to the music.  It's just loud and
pounding, and the people are the same way."  (This was attributed to Shane
McDaid.  Does anyone know him?)

Who needs `em?  They're a former freebie, gone glossy.
Altogether content-free, advertiser-driven rubbish. Stiff
on the SOMA = Soho legend of '86.  Let them interview club
doormen, sip martinis laced with cocaine, and hang themselves
with a velvet rope for all I care.  An interesting "anit-rave"
article could be written someday, along the lines of (what) will
people learn from rave energy anyway, how can one have worthwhile
conversations at 110 dB's, and whatever happened to other types
of free time.  But if *they* wind up writing it, why, I'll eat
my whistle!

RetroYob

bob wilson wrote /the illuminatus!/ trilogy, /wilhelm reich in hell/,
/prometheus rising/, /coincidence/, /cosmic triger/ and a host of other
good books.  he is associated with the psychedelic movement; he was a keynote
speaker (along with tim leary, francis huxley, paul lee and terence mckenna)
at the bridge conference at stanford a couple of years ago.  (the bridge: 
exploring the past, present and future pf psychedelics.  a very cool 
conference, john lily was there too, d'kookoo, fungo mungo... great to 
actually drop acid with all those *guru's*)

anyway, wilson is a really interesting guy, existing in many realities at
any given moment.  he helped start the whole 23 thing.

he currently lives down here in capitola.  his number is listed.

rocky

To: sfraves@soda.berkeley.edu
Subject: Osmosis was the mostest
Status: R

(enter self-kick mode)

Why on earth did it take me nine months to discover Osmosis???

(end self-kick mode)

This was one of the finer club raves I'd ever been to (prior mood:
average.  total substance intake:  one beer).  The mix of both people and
music was as varied as you could imagine.  Both dance floors (in adjoining
rooms) were well packed with writhing bodies.  The layout of the
third floor at DV8 provides more nooks, crannies, and changes of
scene than any local venue apart from the Jack London Club / Floppy
House.  Maybe the fact that this was the final Osmosis made it better
than the average one, but I was impressed, and left most reluctantly.

I'll post a few new flyers I found there in a bit.

Oh, and I talked to Joel, who is supposedly *the* promoter of Creation
this weekend (formerly a principal of Rave Called Sharon).  I told him
of the bitter disappointment of the last two way-out-of-town raves
(Saratoga Springs and Woodside) and hoped out loud this one would be
different.  He assured me that the Santa Rosa police know about it
and are completely cooperating (?!).  In any case, he confirmed my
hunch that noise (no residents anywhere nearby) and parking (room for
over 2000 cars!) aren't going to be a problem.  He expects between
3 and 4 thousand happy ravers to attend.  Count me in....

- MykL G

Robert Anton Wilson is a writer, philosopher, futurist, and psychologist,
among many.  he may be best known for writing the Schrodinger's Cat trilogy,
and with Robert Shea, the Illuminatus! trilogy (scifi).  his non-fiction
includes Quantum Psychology, Coincidance, Sex and Drugs, and Cosmic Trigger
(vols. 1 & 2).

he's been a stand-up comic, and was an editor of Playboy for some five years.
i expect he'll be an interesting and entertaining speaker.  he may talk some
about his most recent book (released in april), Reality Is What You Can Get
Away With.

the talk is this saturday, 10pm, 174 king st in SF.  ticket includes admission
the rave there afterwards.  415 995 4936 for info.

Robert Anton Wilson is a writer, philosopher, futurist, and psychologist,
among many.  he may be best known for writing the Schrodinger's Cat trilogy,
and with Robert Shea, the Illuminatus! trilogy (scifi).  his non-fiction
includes Quantum Psychology, Coincidance, Sex and Drugs, and Cosmic Trigger
(vols. 1 & 2).

he's been a stand-up comic, and was an editor of Playboy for some five years.
i expect he'll be an interesting and entertaining speaker.  he may talk some
about his most recent book (released in april), Reality Is What You Can Get
Away With.

the talk is this saturday, 10pm, 174 king st in SF.  ticket includes admission
the rave there afterwards.  415 995 4936 for info.

" ...don't worry, the rave just keeps going along in your head til the
" next place...

I definately had a lot of fun Friday.  I went eight different places
where I met people here and there -- if I include early Friday morning
and late Friday morning.

The EndUp Thursday evening was very friendly.  Osmosis was really
good.  A Town Hall Meeting was interesting enough, although definately
not rave material.  N Zinga was a necessary change for me at the time
-- Fridays are my tired days.  If I had the money I would have gone to
that big one called Reach Out!, but instead just hung out around all
the different map points -- that was fun!  Then I went to Felix the
Cat, hot and sort of mixed crowd but still fun; Big Heart City was
later than I wanted since an hour went by before they opened, but when
we all got in it was warm and active.  I decided to wander over to 177
Townsend, where I was very happy to dance and listen to Markie Mark
doing very well, and seeing the light system at its best for me to
date.  The End Up Saturday morning was a very nice place to go again,
very varied crowd and sort of talkative once I break down the barriers
of meeting people.  Tonight I stepped in Colossus, stepped out (but
want to go back some day --- just not rave like enough for me I guess)
and then finally right now I'm about to catch the last bit of
Care*Free, if it's possible ... I've had a great time.

Brad

Just picked up Instinct Dance, a compilation off the Instinct label. 
Excellent -- Moby (Go and Mobility) and Barracuda are really good, though not
all that fast, but the Brainstorm and Voodoo Child tracks rip.  Have You Seen
My Baby by Voodoo Child especially struck me.

It's really irritating, though, I hear about domestic techno releases and then
no record store around here has ever heard them, or can order them.  Everyone
on alt.rave is going nuts over Digideroo by Aphex Twin, which is domestic,
but I can't find it...  Instinct Dance and Zoo Rave I (which looks like a box
of detergent or something, allegedly good, haven't gotten it yet) are the 
Eon has an album coming out, don't know when, should be domestic, I'm 
definitely getting that...  Also pashdown@javelin.sim.es.com does a lot of
techno reviews, you could ask him for those, or for recommendations.

-- Alan

Subject: Moscow, Floppy's and going to Townsend late
Status: R

I was thinking this morning how wonderful it would be for Moscow, and
eventually other parts of northeast eurasia to have raves.
While they're going through these hard times, I can see a sort of cultish
thing going on there where raves are really emotionally done well.
In July, Moscow is having a rave (helped out by people from around
here), as well as Japan.

Now, that reminds me of something -- did anyone read the article in
The Bay Guardian, May 13 pg 13 `Pirate Radio'?  It's got a great sense
about it.  It talks about setting up radio stations without getting
the great governmental stamp of approval.  A neat slogan was in the
artical "Think Globally, Broadcast Locally."  There's one local
station in the Mission district called KXXX at around 89.9 FM on
Sundays from 9 to 11 pm, I wonder where else people will set these up?
Anyone want to get one for the Haight area?
  I usually like to stay out of trouble, but the FCC is one beast
which has bothered me ever since I realized they existed -- they
exercise undue control over the content of our lives, as exemplified
in my memory by KQEC, KQED's old sister station which was taken away
from KQED because they aired some real stuff on it.  Now, has FCC been
like KGB and gotten better in recent years, or are they as fascist as
ever still?  I haven't heard much either way.  When I get my own money
I can start to buy my own music, but for now the idea of letting
someone else play me their music which I may find interesting is a
neat idea.  (I already use the Internet and thus have my underground
news needs fulfilled that way.)

I stepped out of my house at 6 this morning, only to find to my dismay
that I had missed a great time at Floppy's ($5 with a great location
across from the CalTrain station -- it was still going when I checked
it out at 7AM but I think I missed the bulk of it).  Care*Free was
hopping slightly when I got there too.  It was fun to run into about
seven people I know this morning -- for me that's making life much
funner, since this is about the first month in my life where I can
roam freely and run into people I know.  It's really fun to make
friends at raves and then see them again and again later.

If I only had an infinite bank account ... (I can manage without, but
lately that's meant I get to go everywhere either by knowing someone
or by showing up really late -- this offers its own kind of
interesting fun moving from place to place, but quite seriously I'd
rather just go and pay a bunch when everyone else is there too).

Brad

From bbehlen Sun May 31 23:31:26 1992
Received: by soda.berkeley.edu (5.65/KAOS-1)
	id AA20549; Sun, 31 May 92 23:27:15 -0700
Received: by soda.berkeley.edu (5.65/KAOS-1)
	id AA20538; Sun, 31 May 92 23:26:58 -0700
Date: Sun, 31 May 92 23:26:58 -0700
From: Vitamin B (Brian Behlendorf) <bbehlen>
Message-Id: <9206010626.AA20538@soda.berkeley.edu>
To: ahawks@isis.cs.du.edu, snyside!dan@sgi.com
Subject: Re:  Techno Music Request...
Cc: sfraves@soda.berkeley.edu

I'll see if I can track down a DJ or two and get their top-20's from them,
maybe once every two weeks or something. Also, there's a lot of techno
talk on the manchester list (manchester-request@irss.njit.edu), and as 
someone has pointed out, pashdown@javelin.sim.es.com has a fairly large
collection of reviews he's done. (Sorry Pete :)  

As far as record stores in SF, I asked a very similar question about 2 
months ago on the list, and all four people who replied said BPM was
the best. I'd have to concur, and maybe add Star Records (I forget the
address) and maybe Butch Wax. On the East Bay, surprisingly enough
Leopold's in Berkeley has a fairly large selection of popular techno
12"'s and CD's (if you get there before I do, he he he:) Rasputin's gets
semi-decent CD's and domestic 12"'s, but the Tower in Berkeley sucks
(but according to miss silverio the Tower in Mountain View has a good
selection). 

There are also a lot of good techno compilations coming out domestic, too
(although they may have somewhat dated music). For $14 at most stores, 
there's
Techno-Rave Vol's 1,2,3
Zoo Rave (the detergent-box look-alike)
Techno Vol. 1
Only for the Headstrong (recommended!)
Instinct Dance 
Guerilla Grooves (more rub-a-dub-ish, but still cool)
Best of STR (harder to find, but has some cool stuff) vol's 1,2

There are some great techno compilations on import; the stores montioned
above would probably carry these, though the chain stores would probably be
better stocked than the DJ-only stores (DJ's, "real" DJ's, seem to have a
phobia about vinyl - I'm going to start buying my singles on vinyl but
still buy the compilations on CD) These import goodies are:

Give Peace a Dance (Vol 3 is GREAT, Vol. 2 is great but entirely ambient, 1's Pok)
Serious Beats Vol. 1-4 (3 & 4 are double-discs; 2 is great, 1 is pretty goodm
		3 & 4 have a lot of good stuff but they've been shortened)

Breaks, Bass, & Bleeps Vol's 1-4 (very good series, primarily if you like
	Kraftwerk-derived fast techno.)

Techno Trax Vol's 1-4 (Highly recommended series, except for 1. If you could
	only buy a few compilations, get these)

1000 Ohm!, 2000 Ohm! - Harder, more abrasive techno, perhaps a bit slower
	than most, but at +6 it sounds great! Lotsa good acidic head-trip 
	sounding stuff.

Techno-Rave! Vol 1, 2 (These are both 2-disc sets, have a more acidic flavor)

Champion Sounds - best of Kickin' (Consistently great, fast stuff - from 
	Messiah's "There Is No Law" to "Xeroxed" by Zero Zero. Very gooood)

Chaos Theory Vol. 1 & 2 (The first half of Vol. 1 is pretty good, and Vol.
	2 is a lot of break-beat Prodigy-sounding stuff (I like))

XL Recordings - Vol's 1,2,3 (avoid 1, 2's killer, 3's again in the break-beat
	house vein)

Finally, there are the "DJ-only" remix services, who issue both CD's and
vinyl:

Art of Mix (going alphabetically here) - remixed for long intros and outtros,
	their ravey stuff begins on Vol. 7 and 8 (but avoid 9, and stuff before
	these are much more "post-modern/alternative") (CD's, I'm talking about
	here). 

Razormaid - bleah! They used to be somewhat decent, somewhat acidic (their 
mix
	of "Turn On" by Psychic TV is GREAT, and RM-CD-A1, -R@, and Z-3 were
	great, too.), but their recent stuff has been s-h-i-t. They're starting
	a new line, called Seismic Sound, which looks (according to a future
	track listing) promising, but their mix of Egma's "Let the Bass Kick"
	sucked. Avoid until further notice. (Sorry Joseph!)

Twitch - Really, really great stuff. Vinyl: Anything Vol. 3 and later is very
	ravey, as is CD 2 (CD 3 is being pressed as we speak). The prices compare
	to import CD and vinyl compilation prices. Contact sybase!mw@sun.com
	for more info. (Hi Mike! Hope ya don't mind). Superior mixes, by the
	way, great for both DJ's and the ordinary home listener....


Phew! That's about all I have time for. I didn't really expect say so much...
sorry if it sounds haphazard. Write me if you want more info about the above.

	Brian

p.s. - anybody out there with a .com domain in the East Bay area need a hard-
working Berkeley sophomore CS major for a part-time (20 hrs/week) job? I
need something to help pay for the music... and I'd like to get work experience
in the CS field. I have too much spare time for my own good. Do I really need
to be reading all 264 articles in alt.religion.kibology? I didn't think so...

My favorite records stores in the Bay Area:

1) Star Records (Hayes Street, SF).  Well-stocked!

2) BPM Music Factory (Polk Street, SF).  Has the latest imports.

3) Leopold's (Berkeley).  Closer for east-bay people for import 12".
	Limited selection.

4) Amoeba (Berkeley).  Good for import CDs and used 12".

5) Record Rack, Butch Wax (18th St, SF).  Not as popular as Star and
	BPM, but they have stuff you might not find elsewhere for
	12".
